[2018-02-25 15:27] <Larsenv> Cracked License Manager for CodeWarrior

Thanks to Gericom for cracking this and riidefi for giving this to me.

After running the CodeWarrior v1.7 installer that's included with wii_development_package, go to `C:\Program Files (x86)\Freescale\CW for Wii v1.7\bin\` and replace `lmgr8c.dll` with this.

By the way, you might want to move the "Freescale" folder to C:\Program Files\, since the compiler will mess up with (x86) in the path name. https://cdn.discordapp.com/attachments/370014159254978570/417417252531339274/lmgr8c.dll

[2020-06-24 13:31] <nitr8> *Wii BroadOn Leak ARM-Toolchain for x86 Linux removed*
[2020-06-24 13:31] <nitr8> *Wii BroadOn Leak ARM-Toolchain for x64 Linux removed*
[2020-06-24 13:31] <nitr8> *Wii BroadOn Leak ARM-Toolchain Buildscript removed*
[2020-06-24 13:34] <nitr8> Reason: Their binary output didn't produce any usable IOS as seen at least according to the disassembly of "ARMBOOT" and while testing: IOS didn't boot at all
[2020-06-24 13:41] <nitr8> Background: The IOS ARMBOOT core does "long calls" ("-mlong-calls" as seen within the IOS Crypto Module MAKEFILE and the IOS "loader" ("ARMBOOT")) which usually are being done during "thumb-interworking" mode, which in turn produces "_call_via_rX" register calls as the registers have the pointer to the function to run into. This isn't the same attempt BroadOn used while developing IOS. Instead of calling "_call_via_rX", they did a "BLX" ARM instruction call which required a patch for - AT LEAST - BINUTILS v2.16. This patch is included within my current Buildscript which almost compiles the ARM-Toolchain for x86 & x64 Linux (as tested on Ubuntu v18.04.1 x64 and RedHat 4 Enterprise x86). Those IOS WAD's do actually run (tested on a "BroadOn Leak compiled IOS53" using THIS toolchain).
[2020-06-24 13:46] <nitr8> The patches BroadOn used for BINUTILS are almost 17 years old according to a commit found using Google and another commit by "Richard Earnshaw" (GCC-ARM "specialist") - found on the GCC CVS archives (which aren't available anymore officially) and bug reports by private users within the BINUTILS mailing list... (pretty old stuff)

[2020-07-25 12:12] <Zora> **How to combine parts together**
__Windows:__
1. Open Command Prompt in the directory containing the parts.
2. Run this command with the placeholders filled in.
`copy /b [part 1]+[part 2]+[part 3]+[part 4]+[...] [filename.ext]`
*Order matters!*
__Linux:__
1. Open Terminal in the directory containing the parts.
2. Run this command with the placeholders filled in.
`cat [part 1] [part 2] [part 3] [...] > [filename.ext]`
*Order matters!*
